<time>1557714973870<//time><Rate>5<//Rate><Text>So you want a dog.  I decided I did and looked in all the wrong places.  While I own a home with a fenced yard, all the rescues were determined to decide on the right dog for me. I wanted to decide myself.  And I sure didn't want a puppy.  So I started looking on Craigslist too.  Someone suggested I try the OAS on a regular basis focusing just on dogs newly available for adoption, since I didn't want a chihuahua or a pit bull/mix.  This is how we met Ivy.  We had one play session and headed back two days later.  On that day we decided she would come home with us.  Let me point out that unlike rescues, OAS fees are remarkably reasonable, especially if you are a (ahem) senior. Ivy isn't  perfect, but neither are we.  She is leash reactive and we have worked on this since we got her.  She is sweet in a dog park, and seems to be smarter than her owners.  It;'s been a wonderful year with her. Give OAS  a chance.  if you are lucky, you will find a remarkable dog before he or she is pulled by one of the rescues, and for a lot less money.< /Text><pictures>[{'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipN5YCVElJ2Grd2YBrO9cwXoR-xvY8m8g5LtUmbj=w150-h150-k-no-p']}]</pictures>< resp>

<name>Mariana Avila Llorente< /name><Time>1616434803262<//Time><rate>5</rate>< Text>
While some of the negative aspects mentioned by others are true, this place is clearly understaffed and it has a lot of volunteers helping out. Wait times can be long, they may not all be on the same page regarding an animal's information... but, you know what? They are trying their best and, more important they REALLY CARE about the animals. For me, that's what matters most. We adopted a 3-month-old cat some time ago, and he's been in great health ever since. I wouldn't hesitate to get my next pet from Oakland Animal Services again.<//Text>

< Review>
This shelter is  clean and spacious and the staff seems friendly and caring. However, they are not as familiar as they should be about their animals. We adopted our dog from them and they told us the dog was friendly with other animals. This turned out to be far from the truth. Our dog is very aggressive with all other animals. Since she is an only dog and we always keep her leashed when out of our house, it has worked out OK anyway and we have had her for 9 years and love her dearly. We just can't take her to the dog park. Also this shelter does not test for Feline Leukemia Virus (FeLV) which is a virus that compromises a cat's immune system and makes them susceptible to cancer and other diseases. My son adopted his cat from them and a year and a half later the cat got a very aggressive cancer. Turns out he was FeLV positive. Since he was an indoor cat and never came in contact with other cats, it seems that the shelter is the only place he could have picked up the virus. It's possible that he had the virus when he came to the shelter. Unfortunately, this means that he may have passed the virus to other cats at the shelter. We had to put him to sleep yesterday and it was so sad. So be aware that this shelter does not test for this virus and you may want to have any cat you are thinking of adopting independently tested especially if you have other cats in your home as this virus is very contagious.</Review>

PLEASE READ BEFORE ADOPTING:
Oakland Animal Services Director, Rebecca Katz is running a very very poor operation, I‚Äôm sad to say. What I have learned from my experience adopting my dog is that:

1.) OAS agrees in writing to pay for medical care during foster, and they DO NOT PROVIDE THIS CARE. They do not have the funds to provide this care because of poor leadership and they don‚Äôt have a vet on staff to even provide this care.
2.) They do not have a regular vet on staff checking dogs, because they cannot retain one (big red flag), so the dogs going to all of these public adoption events (with other dogs present) are riddled with infections. Mine was one of them.
3.) The vets that come in to do spay surgery prior to ownership are discovering the dogs are also sick, needing far more than just a spay when they are received. Then they scramble to provide the last minute care they can before putting the dog in the owner‚Äôs arms for good that same day.
4.) They are telling people AFTER ADOPTION PAPERS ARE SIGNED that the dogs are terribly ill and need extensive, costly care for said infections. They then leave it on the owners to foot the cost.
5.) When I approached the Director, Rebecca Katz, telling her this experience, requesting medications to treat the dog‚Äôs infections, she at first offered to give Lola some extra medications. Then after reading the dog‚Äôs chart rescinded that offer because it was too costly to her.  This woman only thinks of her bottom line.  Welfare of dogs is not her top priority.
6.) The Director then requested I return the dog to the shelter, which she admits cannot afford to provide even minimal care, and said she would find ANOTHER SHELTER to place Lola in that could provide care. This is after the dog has lived with me for a month and has bonded with our family.  That was the solution Rebecca Katz AT OAS was able to offer after this shitshow.  To remove the dog from a loving home, and dump the dog at another shelter on someone else's dime instead of providing her necessary medications.

I'm keeping the dog, nursing her back to health myself despite the ridiculous position I've been put in financially by OAS, and will rehome her myself if costs become an issue.  But I will never, EVER take an animal to OAS.  The animals and the humans deserve far better!!!

#NeverAgain #OaklandAnimalServices< /Review>

< review>
I have had 2 encounters with them and they were great. 1- when I found a dying cat @ 10pm, stayed up with it in my house all night, and drove to OAS in the morning to have them try to save it. I waited outside for about 20 minutes and an employee showed up. They took the car and my info and I left. They then called me 4 hours later to let me know that it had passed away while under vet care. It wasn‚Äôt even my car. Very sweet of them. 2- an opossum was hit on Fruitvale during rush hour 7am and was still alive trying to crawl to the side of the street. I stopped traffic and scooped him up in a box and called the Oakland police non emergency number. They got ahold of an animal control officer from OAS and he came and got it within an hour. The place wasn‚Äôt even open yet. Great service for such an understaffed group trying to serve all of Oakland. For you disgruntled folks; just like an emergency room I‚Äôm sure the calls are triaged, so the dog that chased you as you ran through the park might not be a top priority when other animals are in distress and dying. 5 stars from me!< /review>

<Date>1580678451562</Date><gmapID>0x80c29512da6dd7bd:0xa3885ca8dc2c580a</gmapID><Response>None< /Response><Rating>1</Rating>< text>
This place is VERY unprofessional. I went in with my dad today expecting to go in with him. I had been to this place before ( about half a year ago ) and was treated really nice, and even been told to come back whenever since I wanted to learn how to handle different types of guns properly. This was my second time going back with my dad who had been coming to this range for around 20 years. The moment we went in I immediately felt the worker target my dad as if he was some sort of danger. He gave us a "safety check" that the guy before us didn't do. They asked him to treat the ammunition in the gun as real ammunition and to unload a loaded gun without breaking any safety regulations. The worker loaded the gun and my dad unloaded the gun facing the ground and gave him the bullets. The worker proceeded to tell him to "try again and remember that everybody in the room counts". He did it again the same way, just more attentive to the way he was doing it as he didn't think there was anything wrong with the way he was unloading the gun. The worker then accused him of "pointing the gun at him TWICE" and kicked us both out saying he couldn't rent out a gun for us. There are no written rules and there wasn't a manager to talk to when we requested it. He kept repeating the same phrase over and over about pointing the gun at others. After going to this place for over 20 years we would never come back. The place discriminates, targets, and has staff that has no knowledge about how to treat its customers. Even if something had been wrong with the way the gun was held, a proper certified instructor would have explained the mistake before the second attempt was made. <resp>None<//resp><time>1508895575503<//time>< text>
After 7 or 8 years of visiting various shooting ranges, I will say this is the indoor shooting range in which I feel the safest seeing as to how they ask every nonmember to demonstrate their firearms safety conduct. If you fail the safety demonstration, they will politely but firmly ask you to leave (so you don't end up endangering other shooters). Before visiting this range, be sure to fully understand and fully obey:
1) The firearms safety rules as outlined by Jeff Cooper
2) The range rules for The Firing Line found on their website
3) How to safely operate any firearm you plan on renting from or bringing to the range

Additionally, their annual membership is reasonably priced and pays off after 9 visits, or 7 visits if you rent one handgun per visit. The range itself is in a good, reasonably accessible location for people living in Los Angeles County, Pasadena, and far east as Rosemead.

Parking: They have 7-9 parking spots in a lot behind the shooting range. There is also street parking very close to the range. Parking was never an issue for me for all of my visits. This shooting range is more busy on the weekends, like most businesses and establishments.

I will end on what I feel is the most important note and I wish there was a way I could emphasize this more but: I am consistently blown away by the professionalism and friendliness of all staff members with each range visit on any given day of the week. This is one of the few ranges where I feel genuinely welcome.</text>

Great sushi but calculate before ordering all you can eat</Text>
< Resp>

<pics>None< /pics>< date>
1492618538103< /date>
</record></dataset><record>
<Pictures>None< /Pictures><rate>3< /rate>< review>
I went here two days ago while visiting a friend in the Long Beach area. Yen has several other locations, including the one near my home in Studio City.

The first thing I noticed when I got here was that this was a Korean owned franchise. Oh no. The menu consisted mainly of contemporary fancy rolls, as well as some other basic "Japanese" food that anybody can learn to cook really. Anyways, I gave the food a shot.

I ordered yellowtail, albacore, and spanish mackerel nigiri sushi. Then my friend got a soft shell crab and salmon roll. After having tried a piece of everything, I concluded that the food here is 3 stars. It's not bad sushi like Todai or Sushi Mac. It's even a tad better than Mon, which is another Korean owned sushi franchise. It's just not on the same freshness/taste level as Noshi Sushi, Sushi Gen, Yotsuya, or even Oomasa. The rolls themselves were just okay too.

Sure, the restaurant interior is nice, clean, and good for friendship outings. But if you want something great tasting, don't drive out of your way to eat here. It's not all that spectacular. I guess now I now how the Studio City location probably tastes like.</review>

<Text>I always take my MB Sprinter van to Mercedes dealers for maintenance because I have always received excellent service:  top notch parts, knowledgeable mechanics who stand behind their work, and extraordinary customer service.  This has proven to be accurate for 3 out of the last 4 MB dealers I have visited UNTIL I visited MB Santa Rosa.

I arrived on time for my appointment to investigate a steering vibration and Matt checked me in.  He was pleasant enough and we had a quick discussion of the symptoms my van was experiencing.  I retired to the lounge and prepared to wait for an hour or so.  About 4 hours later I finally heard from Matt that the mechanic didn't find any mechanical problems with the steering and that this vibration issue was caused by my overly worn tires.  I was surprised to hear this because (a) my tires were not yet worn down to the wear bar, (b) the vibration didn't feel like a tire issue to me, and (c) it took 4 hours to figure this out?.  But this was a Mercedes mechanic, the best in the business, so I trusted them.  Matt offered to sell me a set of 4 tires but the order wouldn't arrive for four days.  I declined because I was under a deadline to continue my drive south to Mexico and couldn't wait around that long.

My van was driven back around front and I was also disappointed to see that it had not been washed.  The three other dealers I have visited all washed my van without being asked, but apparently this isn't offered at Santa Rosa.  I paid the service charge (I guess being told your tires are slightly worn is considered service) and hit the road.  At least if my van had been washed I would have felt like I got a little something for my money.

I called a few shops along my route but none of them had the tires in stock.  Since Matt told me it was just a tire problem and not a mechanical problem, it didn't seem serious so I decided to drive to Mexico and get new tires on the return trip.

On the drive back north I noticed the vibration worsening so I took my van to Mercedes Benz of Van Nuys.  Within about two minutes of arriving, the Service Consultant and a mechanic pinpointed the cause of my problem.  It was not the tires, it was a loose steering linkage located under the hood.  They explained to me how dangerous it was because I could have lost steering at any moment when the bolt loosened all the way out.   They fixed the problem in about 1 hour, happily washed my van for me at no additional charge, and they said it was fine to keep the same tires.  I paid for the service, and the service consultant suggested I contact MB Santa Rosa and ask them to refund their service charge since they obviously missed the problem; a potentially life-threatening problem.

A few days later I called Matt at Santa Rosa, explained the situation, and he said he would talk to his boss and get back to me the next day.  Two days later I still hadn't heard back from Matt so I left a voicemail.  Another two days later, after no response, I left another voicemail for Matt.  I suppose he was hoping I would just give up and go away.  After 9 days and 4 calls to Matt with no response, I changed tactics and got a hold of Lisa in service who seemed genuinely interested in helping me.

Sure enough, later that day I finally got a call back from Matt and he regretted to inform me that since they actually provided me with a service (suggesting I buy new tires) the service charge would not be refunded.  I protested saying they misdiagnosed the problem; it had nothing to do with the tires, in fact they were still on the van and it was driving perfectly now!  Matt responded that doctors misdiagnose patients all the time but they still get paid, so they would NOT refund me.  I have never experienced such blatantly unethical behavior from any mechanic anywhere, and especially not from a Mercedes dealer.

So, unless you enjoy paying for faulty service that could potentially kill you, and terrible customer service that doesn't return your calls, take your business elsewhere.<//Text>< user_name>
Chris James< /user_name>
</record></dataset><record>

<Name>Braiden Hensley< /Name>< Review>
The wait time is a lot shorter then the 2 hours I remember from years ago. However, if you have questions about anything, if you can't find it online, go in to the courthouse. They have no staff available to answer phones due to budget cuts, even if you are checking your court date. Its better to go in. They have a drop box outside that is always available and they empty it every weekday morning, I think, when they open. If you get to a window and you have something left incomplete, if you can fix it there, they give you a pass to jump to the front of the line as long as you can complete it that day before closing. If you are still in line at 3 PM, they will keep working until all the people in line have been seen, however they lock the doors at 3 PM so you have to arrive before then. There are also metal detecors you have to walk through and an b-day machine for purses. No weapons, drugs, alcohol, even pocket knives are allowed and for somethings the officers will set aside for you to retrieve before you leave. Same process like with any other courthouse. They don't make copies for you and there is no copier or printer available so come prepared. They payment methods are also limited. I think cash and check are preferred but don't quote me on that. Again, DON'T TRY CALLING ON THE PHONE! YOU WON'T GET THROUGH! And if you have a choice, don't go in on Monday. I was told that is one of the busiest days for them and results in long wait times. I think I went in on a Tuesday or Wednesday and they had a good amount of Windows open and the line was moving pretty quick. Even though when I arrived I had to stand all the way at the back door of the building. I was seen in way under an hour, probably about 30 minutes give or take.<//Review>

So my first experiences here were good. I got a dog vaccinated and examined, a cat vaccinated and spayed,  another kitten that I fostered examined, and finally our own kitten examined (the vet at that time was really wierd) . Personally I loved Dr. G.  Today I got our kitten neutered and feel ripped off. Brought in a coupon for a $30 neuter. Opted for, what I was told, the pain meds at $59 and $18 for antibiotics. My hubby loves his kitten so I went for it. Picked him up and brought him home. Realized they didn't give me the meds. So I called and went back for them. And to my wonderful (not) surprise, they tell me that the antibiotics were not necessary. But the $59 is not refundable because it was part of a package to cover the I.v., fluids, and catheter. Wait, how is that not part of the neuter cost at $30? And if it wasnt, shouldnt they have told me that this a.m.?  And because it wasn't the girl who ran the front desk when I dropped him off,  the girl Wouldn't help me. After years of decent service, I will never ever go back. $59 is a lot of money for us, so I feel kind of ripped off now that I dont even have the pain meds I opted for. Unfortunate situation, be aware.< /Text>

Salinas only had one Vietnamese restaurant and it wasn‚Äôt all that good, and then God listened to my prayers! And Saigon Noodles opened! At first I thought it was never going to open! They had the coming soon sign for ever!

Then one day I passed by and it was open! Great beautiful people working there, met the owners who happened to be wonderful. This restaurant is just like the ones in San Jose! Really great tasting food!

I am a pho enthusiast! I love it from the first time I ever tried it more than 30 years ago, you get a huge plate full of noodles with mystery meats (I had no idea what they were at the time, now I know) and it all tastes great! They have a seafood pho! It‚Äôs fantastic one of my favorites!

This is a must! You have to try the avocado smoothie! By itself is really good but they also add this thing called buba (!?!?) is like little bubbles of culinary heaven, they have the dark ones and the white ones, they are all great!

It is family owned, be nice to them, be patient, they do tend to get busy and you will be treated like royalty! From the cook in the back the person collecting the dishes to the wait staff, they are all fantastic and friendly and determined to make sure that you have an incredible experience.</text>

< text>
This is a neat and tidy space for storing items. Units are a little small, but they are tall and there seems to be plenty of space for storing. I am renting a 5x5, but the do have larger. The place is extremely clean and well managed. Dan, is helpful and helped us move our stuff into our unit, which was really quite nice!  The only advice I have is if you are wanting to get the one month free deal, sign up on the 1st of the month, if you do not do this, you do not technically get your first month free as you will be charged the within the same month, for ex if you sign up on June 10th, you will be charged on July 11th, even if you have only been in the rental for 31 days, however this can easily be remedied if you booked on the 1st of June, then your first billing would be July 1st, allowing June to be your free month. I ended up paying in the month that should have been free because I signed on April 28th, then was billed on May 29th, but other than this misunderstanding I had, the location is great, the place is well kept, Dan is very helpful and readily available to help you with whatever you need. The process is easy and everything was completed in a matter of minutes. I do recommend this location and working with Dan!</text>
